O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book that is the essence of medical knowledge together with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with this work, which is part of the art of hands, that is to say, surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the art of hands is practiced in our region and is strange to all, it is perfect in its science and ability, and there is nothing left to be added to it by the great books of the ancient ones that have moved the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and the intentions are closed, and the science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	I believe that I will bring it to life with the order of this doctor according to the path of exposure and statement and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of the tools of cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the statement and preparation of him, as is appropriate.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our land, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with it to surmount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and connections and separations of nerves, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of vessels, and the movement and resting places, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, as Hippocrates says, that nothing is with the hand and without work; and more especially in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you in the introduction of this book that he who is not acquainted with the things before stated may fall into error and harm men; so that I have often seen many of those who engage in this science and abandon themselves to it without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of the neck; so that much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another foolish man who carried a stone for a man of Eage, and the stone was great; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and he died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen a lunatic who was called to pull out a tooth; and I saw the state of the lunatic and the size of the tooth, and if they had pulled it out, he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see. I will tell you another story that happened to our country's duke, who had his leg broken and got hurt because of the break. The ducer's ignorance forced him to stretch the break over the wound until it healed completely; he left no scar on the wound, and then he left it like that. He ordered him not to loosen it at all; he waited so long that the leg became whole again and the bones healed, but he came to his end.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate his leg; and when I had dislocated it, it went in peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of corruption were confirmed in him, or his member, and he could not heal it; and the corruption did not stop from going through the member until the members were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see. Another story of a abscess that got rotten and then inflamed because of its lord's wickedness.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is purulent with melancholy humor, it only comes when one touches it with iron if it is not in its proper place that we can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, gentle son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into .ij. divisions: namely, where there is danger in many arrangements; and I will show in each of these divisions of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, you must keep it secret so that the foolish man cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons with skill, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the better path so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are free from these illnesses; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and believe in yourself so that you can go from this world to the other one of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galiens warns against some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of a bad disease unless you are called to be a fool."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to .iij. chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire cautery and water medicine, and the next chapter is about ordering meat according to the season; as well as forms of instruments, and iron tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about tailoring and sewing, and piercing, and suction cups for wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; as well as ordering the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torments, and similar things; and it is ordered from the master as much as necessary to cut off, and the shape of the tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work, it is necessary that I give the quality of aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and the most secret responses; and many wise men would speak on this, and agree upon it; and I am lacking in words, for I shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that universal aid cauterizes all complexeions or matter: that is to say, warm complexeion and dry matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together with matter, some say there is great help in cauterization; and others say the opposite: that cauterization does not help in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the natural power of fire if it is hot, and should not be cured by hot diseases from heat, nor from dryness; and he who said the opposite, that cauterization does great help to hot and dry diseases that come in cours in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found this by trial.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And any way, none but he who has tried it, and who knows by long experience the use of the caustics, and the diversity of complexions in men, and their predispositions and causes of their illnesses, and their cures and the space of time; we have no fear of other complexions, however, for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this will agree and accord with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery is better when it comes out of the cure, and is of greater benefit than fiery medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes not forth but to the limb which it killeth, and hurteth no other member for none name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The burning medicines come from one limb to another in removing, and bring to the limb diseases of grief healing; and by chance they harm the sick.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and because of the goodness of its substance, does not cause this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And because I have found it by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and because it is based on the truth of things; and because I beg your pardon for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it dispels diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his demonstration; take it into your mind.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made in what time the cauterizations should be performed, and be prayed for.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, for because the harm that comes about is alleviated by the aid of cauterization; and most particularly, the cauterization is for necessary pains that cannot be delayed until a greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I do not think at all, son, as they do so; for because the illness that is healed by cauterization does not return; and it serves thus: but it is not like that of which they believe, for because cauterization is only medicine that changes the appearance, and dries up the humors that cause pain, and is more effective than medicine due to its speed, and its virtue, and its dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And one can choose that the illness does not come again according to the appearance of the disease and its place and its virtue; and are gathered in it the excesses by the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless cauterization is administered in the place where there is excess and moisture, as cauterization of fire for the pain, and the similar things, and the pain does not return again; but that happens sometimes.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that the fire cautery is called the medical derriers, and this is true; but they do not believe that fire cautery is worth anything after medicine, but their intention is false, and the fire cautery is the medical derrier because when we administer ways of curing in any disease and they are not worth it, then we administer the cautery to us, and it is worth.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And therefore understand well that the fire cautery is called the medical derrier, not at all according to the intention of the foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And the ancient ones said that fire cautery is an instrument of gold and not of iron, and they did not say about the quality of gold and its height of substance; and they said that the head of the cautery does not cause ulceration, but that is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that in some people it does; and fire cautery of gold is worth more than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And however when you heat an instrument of gold, you are not as if it were heated by the color of gold, and it is often cooled down; and if you heat it too much; so do to fire; and in this way there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter until the end, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery: For the olive oil cautery, pour olive oil onto the scalp and hair, and let it remain for three or four days. By this means, a disease called "soda" is treated, and by the cold and moisture of the hair, ears, and the whole head, and especially by many dreams and pains of the head and teeth, and above all, by all diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a resolute medicine, which doth clear the head.iiij., according to that which is fit for his virtue and his age and his custom of disease, then do thou make ready the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place it crosswise between your hands, and put his hands on some stones; after that, place the root of your thumb on the root of his nail between his two nails; and let your two fingers come together, so that it bleeds from the top, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which there is this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the ink mark, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in turning it over; then let your hand rest, and measure the bone little by little; and if you do not see the bone, then start again with the cautery as I told you; after that, take 1. poc of string, and put it on and make it soft with cotton, and place it on the mark, and leave it 1.iii. days; after that, put cotton wet with balm on it; and let it be until it is heated; then cure the wound with the medicine which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And say the ancient, that as much as the wound stays open, so much more is it purged; and for this reason if you help it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should let the fire cautery be as long as part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and let it be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other said that one should let the cautery be as long on it, and push so hard that the humors go out through it as women put in their veils to let the humors come out; and one must keep the wound open for a long time; after which one must cure and bind.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterizing seem to me neither good nor bad in all things, except that in certain men where there is a risk of pain; and it seems to me that I should let it be; for the head, it is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we witness with other members; and even more so when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first application of cauterizing seems to me safer and milder to me, and from this one uses the assembly in a salutary way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all the head is painful and lasts a long time, then you must use yeris and pills which are called "cochie", and head rinsing and oils and poultices; and if you do the cautery that we have said above, and it doesn't work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize it with fire a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made a fire cautery on each horn of the head as we have said above, and made a cautery at the base where it is called "vasselz", and you place a ventouse there; and align your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary that the cornes cauteries be smaller than those on which we make a cautery at the base of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head there is sudden pain, and it extends to the oil, and the headache is purged by medicines that destroy, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: so then the cauterization is done according to.ij. ways, that is to say, with medicine that destroys and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and it extends to the oil, and the headache is purged by medicines that destroy, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: so then the cauterization is done according to.ij. ways, that is to say, with medicine that destroys and fire. For the fire cautery, squeeze a handful of aloes, and peel off the skin and cut it into .i. pieces as many as.ij. cuts, and then apply the aloes to the scalp or the hair where the pain is in a part that you can reach; and when it has been applied, let it lie and tighten well and leave it so for 10 hours; and then remove it and treat the wound with garlic, and leave the wound for.ij. days or.iij.; then put cotton soaked in butter on the wound as much as possible to heal it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans. de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery

If not, begin cauterizing again, and otherwise as you need, and leave it .iii. days; after i put cotton wet in oil on the wound, and cure for drying up of the wound as long as it is healthy, and if .xl. days pass that it is healthy, then put medicine corrosive water as soon as the bone is uncovered; and treat according to what came out in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	I have a way of cauterizing a fistula that no one of the ancients spoke of. Understand a fistula, and cut the place; then put in the incision 1. a fine saw of wood so that it is shaped like this:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and i make it of the quantity of 1.Z. of lead; and hold your hand firmly where the camahan is, and do not move the patient at all so that the melted lead does not run to its oil; and if you put cotton wet in oil or in alcohol on the patient: the lead, thus placed at the place of the fistula, and heals with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat

dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth

When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then put the head of the disease in your mouth; after heat the cautery so that its form will come out here afterwards in a way that you put a chain on the tooth; and insert the cautery hotly, and hold it until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after release your hand and start the cautery according to your wish; after fill the mouth with salt water, and leave it for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a way the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gums are softened, restrained, and dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the teeth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu. des scrophules	from scrofula

Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is a fistula, and it seems swollen and moist with corruption, then provide the tentative remedy in its place according to how much of it has entered, and keep the fire burning until the flesh that appears to be rotten is burned, one time, or two, or three times, according to the amount of the substance; and watch for the nerves that are in it, and do not make a fire there except in the charnel, and think that it is not forever; after heal the place until it is healed completely, and if the bones have been burned, then know that the fistula is threefold, and the bone at the root has腐った;and thus as one of these that we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of frost comes with strong wind and does not take a woman's talent, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery on both sides of the rain with the clove cautery which we have said before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be .ii. cauterizes in a line, and they will do more good.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from frost and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then it is necessary to make a cautery on the underside of the bladder, where the hair grows on the tip of the finger, and 1 at the right and 1 at the left, each as long as a nail; and make 1 cautery on the back, where you need it, and let them be clove cauterizes according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the breasts
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, it does not allow the seed to develop, and the flowers are corrupted and late in coming; and when they do come, they cause great pain: therefore it is necessary that they be made. 2 cauterizations around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and 2 cauterizations on the back; and let the cauterization be clamped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip joint, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the sign is that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints are found to be hot, so it is necessary that you make a cauterization on the hip joint on the front side towards the joint, and mark in front of the joint as it comes back, so that the joint is inside the circle; and if so, let the cauterization be like those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cauterization is not present, make 2 large olive-sized cauterizations, and let the cauterizations be made in the same way as all the others; and care for it until it is well.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the disease with large humors of foul pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery, and the method of the cautery is according to .ij. methods: that is to say together with medicines that burn, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to mouth of methods, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip joint .iij. cauteres triangular according to this form, and do a good depth and broad, and have between each cautery the thickness of a coin, and be the cauteries olive-colored; never is done cautery in the middle on top of the chief of the hip, for there are .iiij. according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery with the cautery of the circle that we have just mentioned in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in a partial manner so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the spaces of the joint are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li épaisseté dou keur; et se li Malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	Here is the translated text:
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I have also seen many who have made cauterizations on the ankle bone of the foot, and left them so long that the leg was entirely bent over, and the foot as well, and it became infected and corrupted throughout; after which a solution of the stomach brought about death.

And let it be heated until it is all red and warm, and then put it on the hernia's box, and let it be turned around the lower back; and let one cauterization be made and leave three days; and then make an ointment of butter, and let the open wound heal for a long time; after the curative care until it is healed.

Al-Bākhī says that we should use a little of this cauterization because of the fear of its regurgitation, and we should not often use it; and yet this is a good cauterization, which can bear it, and leave it where it burns.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of two
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by sitting down or by impact or by too much evacuation, or by the appearance of expanded cold material, there are no remedies for these unless it is from an infusion of cold substance.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate that this person who has pain in the back, or by sitting down or by impact or by too much evacuation, or by the appearance of expanded cold material, there are no remedies for these unless it is from an infusion of cold substance.
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease affects small children, and the signs of its onset are that they become stiff when they sit up and cry; and you find in the last spine of the back and the appearance that comes on the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	As you see this person, and when you have treated him, if he is burned by fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the fire cautery is applied to each part of the spine evenly; and if you see, then cauterize within the spine with a burning cautery 10 or 15 lines in length, so that the hairs are close to one another. After this, treat it until it is well according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to gangrenous flesh which may be in the nerve's span.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints comes from moisture that spreads to each limb member, and when pain arrives in pieces, which is properly called "podagra", and when it is caused by cold and can be cured with medicines, then it is cured by fire cautery in this way: Make a fire cautery within the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if he needs that you hold on the face of the foot, do a cauterization with all the cauterizations that are claimed "point". And if the pains come up to the genitals and other joints, and this happens many times, do a cauterization on each kneecap .iiij. cauterizes or .iii. cauterizes of each part, at all the olive cauterization; and if you need more, do more, but don't hold your hand firmly except for as long as the flesh of the knee is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend up to the knees and back, administer the cauterization that we have said in his chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, do one line; and if there is still pain in both, do one on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and govern well the patient and take medicines. For if you govern him well and you make him sweat, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the cut of the surgeon
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the cut comes in the angles, and the boll becomes hot in the coions and this is newly, then it is necessary that when you see him cured, he doesn't leave him there; and he uses things that moisten his belly, so that the end descends from his belly; after that, he makes him sit down on his back between your hands, and orders him to wet his hair until the boll is repaired, and he brings it to your hands, and signs the cut above the knuckle of the hand, and all in a shape like half of a circle over the chest; then you heat the cauterization as follows:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	For as long as it is white and has a soft touch. Then return the balls to their place; and let the minister hold his hand so that they do not turn back; and well treat the legs of the patient, and put on him 1.i. a cussin and 1.i. an attendant on the legs, and 1.i. another on the loins which hold his hands; then place the cautery on his mark throughout your whole hand, and keep it steady and keep it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then begin again with another one until you come to the bone; and take care that the ball does not escape when you are doing the cautery; that you do not burn it; and so that by this the patient does not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you come to the bone with the cautery, your efforts are worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and that of adult people also great according to their measure; after 3 days cure his wound with the butter cautery as long as the burning is osseous; after the cure, treat him with other oilings as long as he is well, and lay him on his back for 10 days while the wound is properly healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be loosened after a long time, so that the ball does not escape when he gets up to go to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 10 days, when he wants to get up, a well-made bandage is laid on him, and it is kept for another 10 days; and he should have good rest, that he work little and take care not to drink too much or eat too much, and do not eat too high food; and when he observes this teaching, he is completely healed. And I will tell you here after the cure of cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of a rupture from the belly

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis. de meselerie	Here is the translated text:
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Here is the translated text:
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if he feels pain everywhere, and it becomes obvious that you must treat him with these cauterizations that we have spoken of at the beginning, namely: cauterize in his navel, and two cauterizes on the spine of the neck, and seven cauterizes on the spine of the back, and one great one on the crown, and another little one, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the breastbone, and three on each hand and foot joint, and two in the palm of the hand; and be careful not to burn the hair that is on him, so that you do not cauterize over the bones of the hands and feet, nor the liver.
