de squinance	of squint eyes
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	the old used to speak of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and this is their writing about it.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint eyes, it is necessary that the incision of the throat, which is called "epiglotte", be cut out; and one should not do this except for someone who has a cold in his nose or mouth or in iij. Mandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the throat canal, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte so that the danger of strangulation does not come from it.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is then necessary when we want to split the epiglottis that we do so with a pair of scissors .iiij. A small cut through , between the iiij. circles or by the quantity of the cut in the soft part, not into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those are suitable to the cutting of the epiglottis that there is no charnel, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to all its length, then split the larynx as far as it comes to the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the soft part, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and is demonstrated by the cutting of the stream of the larynx that jumps out through the place that has been broken, and by the absence of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt the strangulation, bring together the .ij. lips of the wound and the whole heart under the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce a warm feeling, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuças says: “Do not do this yet as long as the throat is all stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the shortage causes him to pass away.”
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot pass away, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and so the elder commanded that the wound be left open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it has passed in iii days or iiiiii.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch the wound and heal, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and put it in her throat, and went out through the charnel gate;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and I found it as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that flowed from it, and I see well that it had not yet opened a vein or gone deeper than the throat, but its course was through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it as well as I could;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the maiden had only a red voice, and returned to her own disposition;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for I know of no pain in surgery of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	are called "gorge hernies", and are large hernias in a shade of yellow, and are common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and are according to the following manner: natural and accidental; or, naturally there is no disease.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And this accident happens according to .ij. ways, of which one is resembling fat us, and another way is resembling abscess that comes from us by arteries;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it has fear, and does not come to operate fire furiously except in the one who is small, and proves and searches at all the infiltrator:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it also as fat us, and cannot in any way, if the cap, if he caps us, and carries all his cap, if there is no point;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well everything, and cure if it comes, as it should, completely healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and so it is necessary that I state the entire difference between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is hot and fiery, until the bubbles have passed, and it is complete; then rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the cold there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains water, which is a bag of its own stuff, and it begins like a nut, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, whether fat or moist, and of all colors as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the cure of the cold, you should first test and inquire about all the instruments that are called "intramossoires", according to their form or paste which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way to test the abscesses is that you press or more moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the cure, then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull out the intruder, and take care not to put it back in again.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the runner is running quickly because of moisture, make its color as I said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the intruder there is no moisture, know that it is greasy, so you do it crosswise and take it with tongs, and scorch it lightly on each side, and leave it where it lies, so that you may get a healthy meal from it.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot get it out whole, take it in pieces so that nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if I do not wait, he comes back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if he delays for a little while and does not harm me, I will pour corrosive water powder on the wound, extract it, put warm wax on it, and apply soothing ointment to it, and treat it with other remedies until it is well;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if we count the wounds, we will count them one by one, and treat those that are sore with oil;
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is against or another place that is difficult and urgent to reach, put on it vitriolic oil, and leave it for 10 or 20 days, until the wound stings, and then return to the cup where it was delayed;
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	See here the forms of instruments for insertion, and they are of three kinds: large and small and tiny; and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and they are of three kinds: large, small, and tiny, to encircle abscesses of fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used for piercing sorceresses, and they are of yellow gold, or iron, or silver, and those that are red are more proven to break black balls in order to encircle the furrows of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: large, medium and small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the apertures.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of needles are of many appearances, as you can see here: large, medium and small; and if there are needles that have 3 quarters of different kinds as well;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if there are one hundred and ten who have three horns and they are also of three ways; and if there are one hundred and ten who have two horns, and one hundred and ten with only one horn, and they are all three ways; and all these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	and the head of these who have are sharp, and such do not cut except on one side, so that we peel them off, so as not to cut the vein or the nerve; but of those who only have one horn, we cut the back of the neck so that we do not cut the jugular vein or the spinal cord.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and these intrusions are the almeils that are turned over many times, so that the patient does not lose his vision at the opening of the abscesses; but of those who have only one horn, we cut the base of the neck so that we do not cut the optical nerve.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three ways: large, small, and middle-sized, as you see; but of those who only have one horn, we will speak about them in the following chapter.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and don't use one more than in place charnut, so as legs, arms, mamelles, and hands, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and don't make one other instrument small, resembling to scabs of fists, according to this form, so that one dries up blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it not once in the place which heals with copiousness of veins and arteries, and never according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	and inflame not the mammary glands of certain men when they become corrupted, so that they seem like mammary glands of a woman:
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they will remain lame and swollen, and who should cure them, it is necessary to do so according to the form of this chapter B until:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scorch the fat, and employ medicine to the wound in charring, then join together the 18 threads of the wound with stitches, and heal it until it is well;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and let him suck the meat raw, and be softened by its size so as to resemble women's breasts, if he makes them in 18 stitches on top, with 18 similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds the other at the end of the one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line B up to line G;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then peel the skin that is between the two lips, and cut away the fat, and add what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary for the treatment, until he is well.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not well, or the incision is not entirely finished, so that the patient does not rest, or for the escape of blood, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton wadded with a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it sit there until the juice and remaining fat have dried up, then treat it until it is well.
des apostemes des asselles	the abscesses of the elbows
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The scrofulous glands that come out of the armpits are handled in the same way as hard scrofula with ribs and those that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	These that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line B up to line G: .i.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels that are in the abscess are empty, then patch it with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment according to this until it is well.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a scrofulous nature, so deal with it as we have said in the section on dealing with scrofula, and if the wound is deep, apply fire cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery ruptures and the skin above is tightened, many times there are abscesses, and also it escapes to the infected vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one incises at its base as soon as possible, if the abscess is long, then it will be completely healed.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it at its two ends, if there is a pain, and when it escapes to the vein, if it seems to move away.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is madness to cut this abscess, and most especially when it is dislocated from the arm and the neck and mouth of others, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment with fire, and that of the head must also be avoided, and in that of inflammation of an artery, cut through the skin above.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work on the waist as with a sharp knife, and remove the arterioles completely, leaving them uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then stretch out a needle, and pierce it all the way to the other side of the chest, and hold back the artery with a double thread of silk, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	and then point out the place that is between the 17th and 18th joints of an intramuscular injection as long as there is no leak from it, and loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	and then apply the poultice that will help heal the wound, as long as the thread still shows;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat with an ointment suitable for this, until it is well;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and the abscess should be cut at the size of the vein, if possible, so that you take hold of it with your hand to all the skin,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then dip the needle in the oil that you hold in your hand, and let it go through, and it has .ii. thread of a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then tie the aposteme, as I told you, or a piece of thread from one of the  .ii. parts to the .ii. chisel with the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, then take another needle with all of the thread tied to the incision made by the first needle, and pull out the threads in   .iii. lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the aposteme as much as possible, then cut the excess of the knot and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then dip in .i. cloth in wine and oil, then administer the cures of tent and onions as long as he is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the ears
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, when they come from the artery and the vein, they come to the abscesses of the ears when they are wounded, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with the shoulders and the arms and in all joints, and this is what causes the abscesses, and its color seems to be the color of the heart, and it is in many states without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they are held in place, if the patient feels pain, and is not completely healed, but continues to improve;
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and mutter well from all sides, and do not move forward or backward, nor above nor below, and the one who is in joints does not come to cover with iron: perhaps there will be a contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or the forehead, they put the skin on the scalpum.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the aposteme is small, if it has a nail, and copes it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the suspension is at the neck, and the scorching, then the bone and joins the wound with sutures, and cares until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	large holes hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	No time has come to the belly and nowhere else except in the appearance of mold by the resemblance of ashes, and is the subtle root and the large tree; and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw. i. home who had .ij. bellies that were more resembling to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were split open, and they ran together with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them and found one weighing .xviij. ounces, and the other .vj. Z., and the openings in the incision so that you see that the patient is moist, and the color of the armpit is pale and moist with a fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the wound is wide, and be in your presence the fire cautery. For the barber comes often too great a loss of blood, and goes away from you, so that you hasten then do the cauterizer;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient sweating and afraid of the incision of iron, then take a well-made string of flax, and bind the armpit as we have said, and leave it for .ij. days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then restrain it, and do not cease to pull the flax string as long as it binds the armpit, and feel through it; and if the roots are thick, so take care to cauterize yourself with fire from the navel, but you can well cauterize half of it,
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	and then cauterize so that it does not return; and then cure the wound, and be careful not to cover the clot which is of a green color and of poor sense and of milky liquid.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess that has become infected, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer below.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound is well
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	as the appearance of the pus comes out as a cauterized wound or an abscess, and it is on the belly and there are some boils, just as it happens in other wounds, or as blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or as windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the sinews and by the exit of the bowels, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and an opening of various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when you press it at its two ends it turns back on itself and returns, and perhaps it is tightened, and increases greatly at the entrance to the bath and due to great work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is by moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, without being restrained; and if it is by blood, then open it according to the quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is by wind, then it is a hot wind at the anus, and the work of opening it is that you look at its appearance; whether it is blood from an artery, a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	If it is necessary that you should leave the cure. For there is doubt and fear if, as I have said to you, I dip an abscess, for the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bile, then it is necessary that you instruct the patient that he dye his hair, and be stretched out all straight, then sign with both hands around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to turn slowly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go into the place that you have signed with all the spit.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then, half of the abscess is cut above all the large hook.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it with a strong thread or a firm silk rope, and let us secure it;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then, with your index finger, extend the half of the abscess on the thread, and cut the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find yourself caught on the thread, let it go, and cut the intestine at the end of the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the boil, take it with an awl, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery bleeds against you or cuts into your flesh, then return to your work and take .ij. needles, and bind them with .ij. threads, and bind the needles around that which you have cut so that you pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in .iiij. places above the needles, and if you see, cut off the needles, and leave the place alone until it putrefies, and destroy the pus itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you cut it when it is soft and putrid, then treat what it deserves, and shave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then heal the joint of what it covers, and weld the joint.
dou chancre	the wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	the wound We have spoken in the division about the appearance of cancer, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how one should avoid its cure; and we say that cancer is transmitted to the marrow, and great care must be taken in its treatment, and the ancient one says that when cancer is in a place where it can be cut off like cancer in mamelles, and in the cuisse, and in similar places, it should be completely removed when it is small and new; and no one has ever been cured of it before me. No one has ever been cured of it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ovraiges, when it is in a place where it can be cut off, as we have said, is that you purge no more than once the black bile; then make it healthy if it has manifest repletion, then affined the bile.i. good place for making the ovraige; then cast your onions or cancer, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood run freely, and squeeze the juice at your hand or at any thing, and if it comes to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize as long as the blood is stagnant; then cure with other cures until it is healthy.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	of dropsyWe have already spoken in the division about the appearances of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure that is done with medicines, and that which is cured with iron: it is only to be used; and one should not touch iron in these .ij. appearances: that is to say, tympany and hyp sarche, for it is a mortal thing; so when you treat this appearance of dropsy called "eclyses" with medicines, and the cure does not help, if you see the patient very weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as flatulence and similar things; then do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has only dropsy, and he is not too young nor too old, then do it this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	lay the patient down on his back and press the water out of his belly by bringing it to the lowest part of the body with your hands, then take the spatulum with its thorns according to this form: And be they pointed from both sides, and always do not make them so deep that they can come up to the intestines when you put them on, and cannot scar them.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy is running towards the intestines: it is necessary that you cut them from both sides straight on the knuckles of the hand; and if the dropsy is caused by liver disease, then your cut should be on the left side of the knuckles of the hand; and if it is caused by mucus, then it should be on the right side, and it is only necessary that the patient lie down on the cut where the superfluities do not run to the weak part.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour water over it, and hold your hand over all the sperm between the skin and the syphac also as when you are parching in quantity of an inch or so; then pierce the syphac until the sperm comes out to the clear water, and this is the spring of the water, then press hard, and pour this instrument with which it is: And it is like a fine silver ring, and is of brass or lightweight copper, and in one part .i. small hole; and where it costs on one side, .iij. holes; and .ij. on the other side, and .i. on the other; and the head is cut off as a feather, and this is the form of the incision which the writers cut with a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, now pour it out on the instrument; empty then half or a third, for if you empty more than it is appropriate at that hour, perhaps the patient will die because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he will shake his palms, or come close to death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the malady mean, and its poulz; then treat the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held back now by the cure that stops the hole which is on the syphac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this way; then recommence the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering this, and treat with a little quantity of water:
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do not work any more, and guard yourself from overwork while there is still a little moisture. And if you doubt about the patient, and you leave water there, let the doctor cure him in the earth or sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and let him abstain from drinking; and let the doctor cure him with drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize his stomach and liver and spleen after extraction of the moisture, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of semen
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	No child is born with a small foreskin or one that is not in its place, or if it is, it should be cut according to this form: then put a small foreskin of cork, and tie it up and keep it there for iiij. days or iiij. nights, and when it has urinated, take off the foreskin, and let it urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it does not cover it at all, because the urine that comes out strongly does not leave the foreskin closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	The foreskin should be cut according to this form: then put a small cork foreskin, and tie it up and keep it there for iiij. days or iiij. nights, and when it has urinated, take off the foreskin, and let it urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps it does not cover it at all, because the urine that comes out strongly does not leave the foreskin closed.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of this work is that the patient lies down on his back; then the head of the penis and the scrotum are to be cut off at a size like a feather; so that if he pricks in the middle, as it should be; and be careful not to damage the blood vessels which come often, and if they do, let the blood flow from those who make the blood flow, and cure the wound until it is well.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	come often there are blisters on the penis, and it is an ugly appearance; and some are malicious and others not; so that you must pluck them with a fine needle, and cut and peel them all, then put cotton wet with Egyptian ointment in patch; then cure with diafinicon until they are well.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blister is malicious, of black color and putrid, then you must bring a fire cautery. When you have cut it, and if the blister is inside the skin and part of it is outside, then you must take the blister that is inside first; and when it has hardened, then cure it outwardly. For when you cure it all together, if it is not properly secured at the base of the penis, it will come off, and blackness and corruption will come out of it; so that you must cover everything that is black and corrupted, then put honey and flour on it which is made from the skin of pomegranates and dates, then cure with other cures until it is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if the blood rushes out, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterizations aid in all nine dispositions together: that is, at the rush of blood and corruption. And if the foreskin is corrupted and withdrawn, then it is necessary that you drive or conduct a cord of leather from the penis and make the patient urinate; and when the hair comes off at the head of the penis which has not yet been circumcised, either because of a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape with a sharp instrument until the bonds are loosed and the foreskin is freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a difficult thing to devise this, then it is necessary that you scrape with a spatum at the root of the penis and the hair; then carefully separate between nine and ten, and place one thin linen cloth soaked in cold water on top, so that it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	is not dislocation in the event of a continuous wound; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and especially on infants, it is necessary that we do it in the best way possible and as lightly as possible for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old ones did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only that which we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have heard from the most part of the masters and the learned who made circumcision between the ear and the navel, and all a novacle; so it was done because there are 13 threads, and by chance if one is cut on top and delays that one desoles.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or if it is covered again, and the pain is double, and the washing that is from the navel is not yet assured at the tip of the member; and the washing of the nail by chance escapes the iron, and corrupts the work, and often comes so that there is no need of washing, and I have heard.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	For the washing that is done with all force to all the thread I have found the goodness of experience, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Car when you press your hand, if the hair is cut evenly all around; but let the string be well fastened around the skin; and let the method of the first operation be that you make the child think that you do not bind the string tightly around the penis, and then let it rest in all ways that you can.

Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces for cleaning is this: the two joints should be loose and cut at an angle, and the joints should also be as long as possible;
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope. Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant. dou retenement de l’urine	double retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retene of urine is if an operation of stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or charnel, or similar things that we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine does not flow and you see the retention for the stone that is stuck or in the neck of the bladder, so it is right that the patient be bent on his knees; and let him place the feet over the back, and extend his stomach from the part above the back, and restrain the patient as much as he can; and then obliges the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine flows.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use the extraction instrument that is called a "syringue", which has this form: and be of fine lightweight silver, like the feathers of an owl; and its cane is of a palm long and a half, and be fine at the tip.

et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe as long as the bladder is empty, and let the patient remain calm.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or sores come in the bladder, or scorbut is assembled, and you see distilled water and medicines, so do all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and so at 2.30: 1.30 on one side, and 1. on the other, as you see; and let their hair grow long by means of medicine such that it stops well at the root without addition, if we can remove the moisture, and throw when necessary is.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you see the medicine go into the bladder, put the head of the caustice in the moisture, and draw while drawing which is behind; if you draw the moisture to the caustice, and then throw it hard behind; if it enters the moisture into, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema which we use for the bladder: if so:

de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division of stones and extraction together with medicines; and I have also spoken about the difference between a stone in the kidney and all other signs, and that one must act differently with respect to stone in the bladder than with respect to the spermatic cord. And I will now explain this openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder is more common in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder, resembling water in subtility; and when it opens, it rips the patient's scrotum, and makes it jump many times, and then renews itself; and is lighter to cure children until they are 20 years old, and heavier in elderly people, and weak for those who are between middle age and old age. And the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is understood first to purify the patient with enema, to extract all the matter which is in the intestines. For it is not often necessary to seek stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, and turn him over and move him to the dislocation, so that the stone comes out completely from the bladder, and never goes up again; then let him sit between your hands, and his legs be dislocated, so that the bladder is all turned upside down; then feel it and touch it from behind.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. If you feel the stone in space, then hasten to cut it off on top of the stone. And if it does not come at all when you touch everything, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young; and pour it into its base, and feel the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, press on the top; then let it go at the bottom where you feel the cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and command him to extend it in his right hand, the organs at the top, and with his left hand rub the skin that is dislocated behind the organs in the part where the size is made; then he pours the sperm, of which this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And place between him who is between the hip and the fundament, not in the middle but at the cost of the left knee; and let it be right on the stone, and your two are together or at the fundament, and let the size of the traver be such that it is large by defuere, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, and not too big.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	In case the press should be where the fundament is, so that it does not need to work; and know that there is part of stone where there are angles and edges: such is grious to come out; and if there is part which is souez, like a glant, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	So that you make the size larger where there are angles and edges; and if it does not come out, so that you extract it with tweezers which are also like a file at the tip, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put into it a very sharp tool curved at the tip; and if you cannot do this, then increase the width of the hole with a small chisel, and if it is cut, apply vitriole.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. And if it is very large, so that it needs to be softened, and make a larger hole. For 12 things happen to the patient: or he dies, or his urine comes out all at once by the way that the leach does not hold; but nevertheless you try to extract it, or to chip with tweezers, as long as you extract it in pieces;

de la piere des femmes	of the women's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There has come to pass that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens once, the cure is difficult, and is defended by .iij. things: the one is that per adventure the woman is a virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a woman who knows how to deliver herself from the urine, even though she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that we cannot find a woman who knows how to deliver herself from the urine, even though she is married. And the fourth manner is that if the stone in the woman is more perfect than the stone in the man, it is because her stone can be made shorter by a deeper cut, and there is greater fear involved.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need to go to a woman of great skill in this art, and have her not cut the stone, or at least do so very carefully. Let there be a skilled woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to perform what you command in the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and look well whether his wife is a virgin: then it is fitting that he put out his finger or foundation and seek the stone; and if she breaks it, so bind her hand with a bandage, and recommend that she puts out her finger or with the disease, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder shaped.
