Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man aged .xx.. years who had a pain in his leg due to an internal cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as the materials came to the leg, and was escaped by a large abscess, and had no visible cause for opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirrour by their madness overran so much that it overran upon the aposteme.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrupted meat, and became a fistula, and I came out with much putrefaction that all went away bowels and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many mirred well within two years, and I had no skill in the art of medicine.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	For as long as I was called, and I saw a leg and the medicines with which it was cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and he who runs through the gaps with great speed;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body became red when he was young, and had an orange-colored complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then searched all the gaps
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came from the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and I pierced one of the openings as far as I could see a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupted and destroyed, and the corruption went up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what bone it was corrupted and destroyed, and I took care that there was no other corruption, except for the one that I had found;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to heal the wound with powerful medicines, and it cannot be healed;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found continued corruption in the bone, and the socket, and then I held it, and bent it at the joint;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't fit my palm around the end of the bone, and I had to split it in two;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	and then I bandaged it; and he was healed and completely mended,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it does not need to be said again about the work of this chapter except for its weakness of the disease which cannot endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For in the evacuation of blood there was often, but he was completely healed, and
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and he had a hard nose, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary in all things, neither in air nor in coming.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toenail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	is a nail that grows out of the thumb of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Here is the translation of the provided Old French text:
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is dislocated, and we take no care, so that it comes - I mean an abscess develops -
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they cut and dig deep enough to reach the root of the nail, and by chance cut it all out;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion comes up to the bone, as much as it causes painful odor, and the two cheeks are wide apart, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If it is necessary that you cut off all the excess which has been delayed by the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if his nail presses the wound hard, and begins to prick, and bleeds it.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	if you put a rope around the nail that pricks the wound,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pour the wine on top of it, and pour that subtle and light water on it,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining part of the wound burning and corrosive medicines to destroy everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat with garlic while he is still healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	If the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and burn it, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the corrosion in the bone, then cut it out, as it is said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and treat with garlic while he is still healthy.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wild, and sharp, and it hurts a lot, then you must first cure it.

et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the nail does not come off too close to the nail bed, because the patient would feel a lot of pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if there is something, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the palm of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two bones that join in the palm of some men's hands are often completely bone,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by adventure they have one or other bone there, and never have a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and neither of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in some of us at both ends.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,

Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The two types of dislocation that can occur are those that come from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from fire, or from similar things.

Des vils	Of the vile
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The evil are great enveloped wombs full of superfluous melancholiac things, that come from many members of the body.

Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The following is the translation of the provided text from Old French to English:

De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the ground where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance is not at the same time as the legs, and this happens from a porritture that comes off the skin,

puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the legs change color, and the disease begins to spread from the root, like the roots of a plant.

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that come between the hide and the cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	is called in our land "buff disease", because it often occurs in buffaloes,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between leather and harness, and goes all through the body, ascending and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And it smells bad in the joints of the limbs until it reaches the leather where it went, and it jumps very hard;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infected with pus from some humors, as if they come from the inside, wriggling and crawling, and worms or insects that crawl;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And one doubts about its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes out at the top,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	For by chance enters and destroys the oil; and such things happen often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and drained, then only can one do it when it is:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so that one may then lay it upon a firm, tightly woven cloth,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	and then drape it onto the table and work upon it with great care, and you will not find fault with it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if the fire cautery, as long as he dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater harm that it does, if it corrupts the oil, so as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the oil, then hold back its head with a strong hand, and cut it off far from the oil.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use medicine to cleanse the body of infectious substances that cause disease.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and sewarre of viandes enjanrans porriture.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	this disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that affects certain limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it moves from one member to another; and I saw the one that I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then I saw it grow larger like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place and entered into the shoulder, and turned into a worm;
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later corrupted all over the body, until it came to the other breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that she turned inside out all over the body, like I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how she moved from member to member, for I had never seen such a disease move in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I knew of many who wanted to move from one pain to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I don't want it, if I saw it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because her chest was dry, and the veins were exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason it seems that she has a tight windpipe;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not seem to apply to those who are delicious, and who have moist chests and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the wound heals and heals properly, and then copes with it so that the wind is compelled to stay in place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see the hair at its base,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment of this disease, which prevents wind from leaving the body, is like pills that are foul, and pills of seraphim, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the place of their flight.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their shape is that there are those with large tips, and small, and curled, and welded.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have .ij. angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those who do not move at all: or if one member is moved first,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as the brain, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she moves at all in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary for you to wash away the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after several preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely stuck if it has gone through, then follow it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow sticks and pierces the bone, and a surgeon who is on the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a laceration and a swelling and pain in the eyes, and inflammation and pain in the tongue, and cramps and confusion of speech, and vomiting of food.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes there is a loss of smell and hearing; and sometimes one loses the power of speech and speaking;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and跳出潮湿的白色斑点，看起来像昆虫；
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if it is a sign of the plague, so that you do not have the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hurts or hurts, is that it is close to the left breast, and also feels like it is stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if the arrow also sounds like a pestle, and has black blood, and comes cold and cold sweat, and faints:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then we have doubt that death will come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow is that there is no pain around the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he gasps and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces into the spine, then the small ribs ache; and there is great pain and gasping; and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps because some meat has become stuck there.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters anywhere in the belly, and it goes through without any stop in the intestine, then there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters into the bladder, and the urine flows out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if it is struck and its neck, throat, shoulder, shoulder blade, spine, chest, arms, legs, and limbs are not affected according to certain considerations.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow hits in a nerve or artery, and it does not flow out, as I will tell you about my experience, so do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There came to a man with an arrow in his neck or throat at the root of the windpipe:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I removed the fat from the ear on the other side, and he was cured without feeling any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I tried another arrow, which pricked him in the oil fat of the ear, but not the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was returned, and I only got a prick on the tip toward the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and this arrow was great of an azure arc, to all appear lighter than ears; the game was sound, and no ill accident came.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I shot an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and this arrow was Arabic to ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew how to shoot arrows, and I hid them well until they struck, and the Christians were sound.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I shot an arrow at a man, which hit him in the chest or stomach, and I thought he died;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then let it be passed .xxx. days, if not its disposition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the arrow, and shaped it, and pulled it out, and I did not get a bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see .i. home whose an arrow stuck or into, and was the wound sewn together;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and hold the arrow within him, and do not change its natural dispositions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	You will not find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom he shot an arrow into the face, and it was seared into the flesh;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it remained there without suffering great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And trap an arrow at the king of the prince's home, which hit him in the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was a little declining to the right side; and the arrow was all pulled out
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat after she had been lame for three days. When I found the wound, it was very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I put on her a strong medicine, and I did not feel any pain;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt tingling and pain in its right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought this was of the point of an arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on him the plaster of the navel, with its digestive power, lest the navels inflame themselves.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw his arrows.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on him the plaster quickly, and soon relieved the pain, and delayed the healing process for a long time, for the patient.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he felt the arrow .i. within his neck, and I told him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a caustic medicine of water, as long as it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which had set in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied to the wound the caustic medicine, as long as the head of the arrow was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and well overstep the terms of three months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And so I stretched out the wound until the nails came out from one side and the other, and could not pull it out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	And then I stopped wasting time and thought of ways to make tools, until I had made good nails.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to this, when the form of this chapter comes to an end, as I stretch it out and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I know that the cartilage of the nose cannot be healed.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I healed it and then sewed up the wound, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or have I told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your trust in what I do not say, for the book cannot include everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise men compare well little great thing, and on this which is present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Try 9 or 10 work, and nine instruments for the removal of foreign things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the arrows should not be shot from the limbs except according to the 19 ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes up by the way where it enters, is an arrow entering into its flesh, and does not go up again at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go up now, if you leave it until the flesh is rotten inside, and the exit is healed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, if you leave it like this for some days, and every day change its dressing;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it goes up, and if it does not go up, so cut inside all the way to the bone, as long as the flesh inside is large, and then treat it;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes all the way to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said can happen to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it as long as it remains even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes only to the syph, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone of the shoulder, and does not go further than the syrinx,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and let the patient wait a few days without any harm if possible with the machine of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very badly injured and cannot be taken out, then administer tar-water, as I told you; and then treat the joint until it is well.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is buried in the chest so that it cannot be seen, and you want to find it with all your strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then take it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot stop the bleeding from the wound, and for the depth of the arrow.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve or vein, so that the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and if you can extract the arrow, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone is broken at one end and inserted into the flesh at another,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or rain the ears of the arrow, as long as you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you do not break the arrow, but draw it out with pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot draw it out at first, then turn it, for extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of withdrawal makes you hesitate, then apply what we have said in this chapter about the use of the chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and you must not cut the nerve nor the vein, and you may extract the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or hot or cold, or firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow entered.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do that, then follow what the sign tells you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it does not open anything, or where the skin is swollen in a certain place, if we see or feel it:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Taille therefore from above, as long as the tenaculum can grasp it, and then remove it: if it were to jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand roundly, as long as it enters into the bone and expands it, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be removed, let it rest for a while, and then begin the extraction again as long as it can be removed.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a arrow in it, push it out completely.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it needs to be cut, and you must administer an anaesthetic, if administered .i. an instrument sharpens
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the cavity of the tool; and then remove it,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, if you administer .i. an instrument with a point that enters, in order to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches, then it is necessary that you cut all the way through or the venom will come out, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And then heal the wound as he knows how.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or cuts in the chest or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cover it, then cover it, if you cover it;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, because that is the work;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and heal it as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to extract arrows is similar to an owl's beak; thus, this is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do it: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the claw used is also like the feathers of an owl,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For the tip of the arrow, as well as the shape of the claw, is like the beak of an owl,
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of claws for biting and for catching:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one is cured are .xxx, from which the head is affected xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is a list of veins mentioned in the text, possibly referring to specific areas or structures:
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 19 arteries that are in the 19 temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 19 veins that are in the 19 limbs of the hairs, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is under the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 19 arteries that are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the 19 veins that are in lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the 19 veins that are at the root of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins commonly referred to are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cerebral, and it lies on the left side of the neck, and it is called by the lay people "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the motion is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basal parts,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "vein of the finger"; and the basilar if it is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it  "vein of the thigh", and it is above the femur,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that is spoken about, which opens clearly on top of the bursa.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little finger is the vein between the thumb and the index finger, and if it becomes stiff.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot are 3 veins: one is desos the corbeure d'ou pochet de la gauche cote,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are 3 veins arranged as follows:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The treatment for the veins behind the ears is to aid with the ancient cataracts and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, are that you remove the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the spot where the veins are with an aspergy rug; then strip the patient's neck with a vise,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the 12th vein appears behind the ears depending on the head;
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Have them place their left hand on your right, and where you feel the pulse of the left hand, place the right hand.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and pierce through the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand to all the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut off the flesh and the skin, and the vein well .ij. two hands across, and make to come out of blood as you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bind, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The sinews of the .ij. arteries that are in the .ij. temples, if they cause headache and old age,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sodomy, and eye troubles from tears, and a pain in the heart;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the sinew is such that I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and is that the patient pulls out his neck, as long as the two veins open up wide;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and the tongue from both sides, and then sign with the hand;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	and then place your finger on the vein at the base of your thumb, and draw the lance up;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and then place the vein above, and the cup, just as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then take care of the patient, and put two fingers on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it form, and leave it until it is well; and we have spoken about their operation and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing from a frontal vein is as effective as healing from a temporal artery for ancient facial diseases, and it can also help with migraine and jaundice.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient extracts their tongue by twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called a 'fosseur', whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or some other thing, and let out two drops of blood according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then cut the neck of the patient, and tie the vein so that it is well tied and never works with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too hot; and the vein is crossed, for the bone is near, and the flame might break when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood that flows from the two veins, which are in the two eyes, is to be stopped by holding them steady, and with regard to the scrofula, and to jaundice, and to the feverishness of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their blood is that the patient should remove his hair by turning it, without any ligature, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the blood, and be careful with the blood, a little of the long flame, a little wide, for there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, in case of a breeze, then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then lie on the cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The saint of the vein of birth if it is hot to the touch, and suddenly feverish, and facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as headaches and pain that comes into the face, and indeed when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the saint is that the patient strangles his neck, then pulls his vein with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the thin flame long, and put it between the iij. nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well now, and the blood will begin to run.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't over-press it too much, and make the blood flow according to your need, then let it lie for a night, because it is soon restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	This is the treatment of the five kinds of diseases: with leech, in the case of strangulation of the air tube, and obstruction of the nose, and many diseases, and pemphigus, and corrosions, and herpes, and are menial.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of health is that the patient pulls his hair from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient cuts off .i. part,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then heal the long vein a little widely, then treat the wound with fire as needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then patch up the other side in the same way, then stretch out the limbs, and hold back the hair;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not strangle; and leaves him until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	of the health of the animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	helps to prevent pain in the lips, and corrosion of the gums, and wounds on the lips, and pain in the teeth and mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of this health is to make the patient sit before you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	and turn the lip, and look at .ij. veins, which one is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and recognize them by their color, and by the small veins that are black around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	So then take one and the other, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	take the largest of each pair, and do the same for the .ij. veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the cure of sore throat
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Of the cure of sore throat so treat the head when it is sore, and that is to cut off the tongue after treating the headache, and that is to extract from the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the healer are that the patient swallows between your hands before the sun, and the tongue is cut off, and look at each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So heal them both, and do not be too perfect, for soon are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck, which are commonly treated, are treated according to .iij. ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where it is punctured with a strong flame or small olive oil, and called "aneils";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and thin according to the width and stretching of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is named mirtor, and is wide as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is a good work to open the veiny cheeks of thick blood that appear, and which contain thick blood and turmoil.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and is to heal subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The salve of the bazilica, which is one of these veins, so helps with diseases that are sore in the throat, and where the collar, and where the chest, and where the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the doctor to cauterize the wound, and he must bandage himself with a cloth.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes out, if it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be struck with fire, but cut off like an anchor;
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base does not open clearly, if it is necessary to extrude it, and change another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	"and the skin becomes soft to the touch, so that it can be easily burned with fire..."
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	"And if you recognize the place of the pain, then also draw out the arm, that you touch the place as soon as you know the pulse."
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	"Then sign the arm's end, and then hold the arm, and burn the vein with soft fire."
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard against hurting yourself in the artery when you see the joint move, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	and if you see coming out on top as the urine of a child, and the outside is red and thin, know that it is the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	and hasten then, and put your two hands together, and open your two hands from each other, that many times happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	then take hold of the arm, and let it be, and do not move the arm, and be afraid, and do not move it until it is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if he doesn't swell up again, and it comes to him, and the medicine isn't present, if you cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retained one; and stop the swelling.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig tree, and split it, and take one of the halves and put it well together until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If he swells again, it's good; if not, if the medicine, as we have said, the powders that stop the swelling;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the swelling isn't mixed in several forms for the small size of the wound, and the potential of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The doctor will instruct you to let the veins open and bleed freely.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	For this reason, it is composed of the bazillical and cephalic veins, as we have described.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the doctor must wrap the neck tightly with a scarf, and if he cuts too much skin, it will bleed;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient's eyes become swollen and red, and may not heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and the nerve is often opened many times, and if it does not open in any man by its subtility, it is necessary that you heal him with an anesthetized tool; and avoid the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the .ij. nerves, let it be cut long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the cerebral pain, if it helps, that it draw blood from the head, and help to the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal with fire of olive or of silver, because it is the safest of all veins, because it does not burn the nerve nor the artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, the legs of some men swell, if it happens for the first time, but do not suffer harm."
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about a doctor, if it is that medicine is only for maintaining health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent the diseases that are yet to come;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the surgery be done in one of the three veins that run through the head: namely, the cephalic, facial, and basalic veins;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should undergo surgery when the signs of fullness appear after eating, in autumn and winter after dinner, when the repulsion sign appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should undergo surgery on the first day or third day, after two hours or three days each time;
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The saint who is cured of diseases has no determined fever, but when fasting is of a day or more, in all hours and in all seasons.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and do not cure children until they are .xxiii years old, nor women but only every four months up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not cure the old who have passed sixty.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some are cured, in whatever way, it is necessary that he who makes the cure of the intestines with a light enema,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a mouth of fins retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous entrails which are harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	do not heal those who are too soured by meat, nor those who are yvring (sore from riding), as much as it is necessary, nor droydrics (drowned);
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is healed after colic, vomiting, abdominal cramps, multiple pregnancies, childbirth, staying up late, fasting, and all the virility, or by something of the weapon or the heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	and then slowly the humors, so it is fat, through meat, drinks, and medicine, if you have a price for it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then come between or bath, if nothing causes harm, to subdue the blood gently,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal yourself of the wound from the inside out with oil, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect yourself from work, food, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be lying and joining, and may you be healthier than the one who heals, and rub your arms .ij. times or .iij.,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then remove the ligature carefully, for when it is too tight or too loose, he cannot run without it.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with his hands until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then dip the wound in a little bowl of old oil, then place his left hand on that vein to stop the bleeding;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	that the vein does not burst and does not bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings of a viol, and some such that they are plain with windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts it on the flame, if one removes it from the flame, and cannot open the vein, then one is of such;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, if it is too tight a wound, so that the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, if it should begin again a little while later that same person or in hospital, if his legs are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if his hand is swollen, and the patient hopes, leave it for a day or two, and do not bind his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	for in case there are abscesses; do not enter the bath, then begin the treatment if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if his fracture is small, or the bone does not protrude very much, and you doubt that it will come out at all of its own accord, then, in this fracture itself, go straight to the flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and make a small incision, so that his hand is swollen; for this often happens, when the wound is small:
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see a wound, don't tell the patient anything, and put some oil on it because it cools the body's heat, and is soft in this place where the oil is.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and then administer the oil to each wound you treat the veins so that you stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same oil also makes three times and blows out the wind when it is put on the wound; if it is too thick, however, it becomes subtle and spreads out when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there is a large abscess that comes often, it is necessary to wait until the opening of the vein is small; for in this case, when it is opened, there is little blood.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, and put on top of the place an moistened sponge with water and in silk one little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and is good that you do this after the flow of blood from a vein, and if it remains in place after some days no black or green color, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on any thing of aloe or mirrhe, juice of calamus, myrrh, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often happens incision and appearance to the sight of the basilica: put then your hand on, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, that is the appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat everyone with pain according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it run until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it stay until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are flat and have need of blood extraction, let them make a larger wound, and keep the flames wide open;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to treat them gently at first and often; and they must be treated by cutting across and not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of treatment is protected from the decay of blood and the tingling of nerves, and it is better than the long or wide treatment.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for those whose bodies need treatment, it is necessary to give them moistened bread soaked in grape juice; if they are heated, if they suffer from fever, three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, before the treatment, give moistened bread soaked in musped syrup, or honey syrup aromatized with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he sweats at the armpit after the discharge of blood, it is necessary that he drink beer and aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he faints and then recovers, sometimes several times, as long as he continues to faint, so that he recovers little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue that remains continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he faints and then recovers after the first fainting spell, and he has a strong pulse, then he should recover after .vij hours after the first fainting spell, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who will heal from another side, if it is to heal on the second day or third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For it has shed blood within the body which has become heated, and brings fever; if so, great quantity must be drawn, and the breach enlarged enough to let in the probe.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you shall recompense all the conditions of healing, and place your hand upon his pulse as it heals, that death does not come from the probe.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and if this is to happen many times, when the healing has been neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not suit when you see dislocated arm, and make go out blood the second time, and the hole is closed, that you press on form;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if he is curved, that he extends the arms carefully, for that would be wrong;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until he has healed the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is frozen at the base of the arm comes out;
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put there. i. little of salt water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if a vein is pricked, let it be and do not constrict it, as long as the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity demands that blood be drawn a second time, whether in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is drawn in the same way as the one in the chest because it is composed of the same material.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method for drawing blood from this vein is that the patient immerses his hand in warm water, so that his skin turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then make a small incision so the vein is visible, then cut it now, not wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And make the incision wide and cut it well near the joint of the hand, and if you can't get it out, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it's frozen, don't put the hand in hot water, because we put it in cold water more than in hot water;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein from this incision is safer than any other vein, that there is no artery or nerve;
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salt of the salve for the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Draw out the hand, and dip it in hot water, until the vein has gone, if one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and wrap it with a towel, and tie it tightly, and cut off all of it, if one doesn't mind;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't chop too much off perfectly, for the nerve is all exposed then;
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, it freezes up in the wound, and cannot be removed.
