Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgeon should also work on the left hand if the disease is in the left hand, and do the same for the right hand as I have told you.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgeon should also work on the patient's finger if he has all kinds of diseases that are outside the course of surgery,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	If because of the diseases of the mare, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the cuisses and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its health is that the patient drinks some hot water, and rubs on the vein as long as it lasts.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the joint of the foot; and the vein if it is at the ankle, and above the foot go many reins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, beware of the nerves that are exposed, and heal it also by trampling as when one tramples hay; and let the fire go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the nerve cannot be taken out, put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is healed the first time, start the second time above a little hole, for the leech is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle joint, and its sensation extends to the pain in the thigh, when it is caused by a cold.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its sensation is such that the patient gets in or out of the water, and pulls it off his ankle. iiij. It has two turns.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the nerve does not open; and if it opens, so that you can feel it in all ways, and crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is well known that you can cut it, for the leg is long, and it is well-covered by the skin.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't treat it, then there is no rain of him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard yourself from the toes.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much of the blood that you see, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on it and tie it up; now he is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or of air, or of glass; and the suction is applied in one of the following ways: by hurting and drawing out blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which is not to hurt so according to .ij. ways: or it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation that is made by hurting and by extraction of blood so is made in .xxiii. parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all in the head; and others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and .ii. others in .ii. coastes of the neck; and the windpipe takes out the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction of the 21 shoulders; and the suction on the ribs;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction of the 21 arms; and the suction of the 21 legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction of the 21 ankles; and the suction does not treat a wound, except for small veins that are scattered in the harness,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because there is no pain in it, if one does not feel pain as one feels when one cuts a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that they be ministered to, neither with hot nor cold fire, in any illness that comes from overfullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, because of necessity or illness, they must be treated every hour in the beginning of the month or at the end, and in the middle times;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to exhale, become heavy;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who have repulsion and redness on their face and in their head, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have escaped the tongue, and refresh themselves with blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such people, and they see and hear nothing but blood and confusion and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is half-past one in the morning, we order them to breathe out after .ii. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sage of the muscle so helps the greyness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and does not come until the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in place of the health of the cerebral,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not right that those who are of a cold disposition use it or have a skin condition, because this does them much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and thus it is not suitable for those who are ill with cold diseases to use it, nor for those who have a cold head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	and those who are cured of this disease often become confused, and for that reason, the ventouse should be placed a little further down by the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventsation of the wind enters into the neck at the root of the jaw and the base of the tongue, and for this reason it is difficult to extract the tooth.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and in the split of the channel of the pemoon, and in toast, and in repletion;

Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventsation causes great pain in the neck, and blinding, and ringing in the ears, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth.

Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the mouth bring illness to the mouth and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the place of the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the shoulders bring sickness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the neck bring sickness to the same degree as the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For she draws blood from these large veins.

Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup placed on the back can draw out the foundation and sinuses of the head, and cause disease; it must be large and made of leather, so that it has the power to well draw; and by chance, if it is too thin, it will break; and it will make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs can hurt so much, for they draw blood from all the body, and cause old pains in the hips and knees, and the bladder, and make the muscles weak after long use; and bring about early death in many people.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement. Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The medical treatise is a collection of texts that provide guidance on various aspects of medieval medicine. The text you provided is in Old French and appears to be an excerpt from a larger work. Here is my translation:
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Here is the first line of text translated into English:
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	Translation:
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	Translation:
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are employed, as I did in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is appropriate therefore that we say in this book the sum of words and chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and delays on veracity so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or dislocation comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing prevents him from being able, as weakness of the trunk, or disability, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the tension is too tight or too loose; and mild drinks cold wines, and charred oats and hay, and does not drink too much wine, nor eat any grass that fills the joints with blood, until you have no doubt about the appendage being hot, nor about the matter filling the member; if the sick person returns to his normal government which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meat that is fatty and viscous, like cooked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and pies, and cakes made from milk, and cheese, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For too much nutrition prevents the fracture from healing more quickly and more easily.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of old people and decrepit people cannot heal or strengthen themselves according to their nature, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not cure, reset on the broken bone.i. large joints which join the member together, as much as it can enforce it like before; and does not stop all of its work, and because it is necessary to feed it with large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all sorts of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes up, and another that goes down, like the tapping of a feather to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that makes a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has its own engine, and its own instrument for recovery, according to what the memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is caused by the fracture of the bone due to the twist, and open well from the outside, and some at the press of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torus, nor in the touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, it is not broken;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have torque, or a wound, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but put medicines on it that come here after, and then hold it now carefully.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that goes in the shoulder, and are the three parts separated, it is now necessary to put them together evenly, so that the abscesses come out quickly.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses come out, if you leave it for a day, as long as the abscess is calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it evenly on the medicine that you can apply lightly and thoroughly, and know that the restoration of this is easier than that of the other parts; then hold it, as it is necessary to do hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there is a piece of bone broken off, if it is half way off, whether it be hand or foot, or one of the small members of the hand, or two strings, or a string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member back in its natural position, so that when the broken parts of the member are healed, you remove all the additions by which they have been held in place, and be careful not to cause the patient any further pain or injury through your work.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and carefully join the two bones together with the best joints.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel the joint well with your hand if it seems all right; if it feels good, and don't pull it too much, or press it as those who do so through their work; we have often wanted to do this.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are fixed, let the patient not move them, nor while he is awake, nor while he sleeps, nor while he turns himself over, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard that the limbs be so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when there is no pain, then it is well secured, and one should put it in such a position that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard that it be placed correctly, so that there is no tangling when it is reset;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I know that broken members are different in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as breasts and toes and similar things: it is appropriate to wrap linen cloths of soft and fine fabric around them;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as thigh and leg: it is appropriate to wrap a broad and hard linen cloth around them, for the broad linen cloth embraces the whole thick member, and holds it evenly together so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie the limb firmly with light strapping, .iij. turns or iiij. according to the member, and squeeze your hand lightly at all its length, then go up above the break and squeeze less, so that the break then moves a little apart from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage little by little, until you squeeze a great deal of the sound place, then take again .i. other bandage and wrap it tightly above the broken spot;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the sound part of the break, and squeeze it slightly, not too hard or too lightly, as we have said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the light strapping or linen fabrics, until it is all even, then lay it all over .i. bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling;
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or an infection, put something soothing on the abscess, and let it rest for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	and then strain it with your thumbs, and let there be a half-inch length of a broad blade of grass or a twig from a palm tree, or according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the thumb that one puts on the break be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also be as long or short as appropriate for the limb's size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	and fasten to the stakes also as you did with the first one, and then tie above it a thread running, as in the first one on the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and then make it tighter, a little less than before, and the thread should be thin, not too thick nor too thin, and made of linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is too thick, like those used for knots in rope to tie up linen, it is a great mistake, because the line will not be equal if there is too much space between each stake; and it should only measure about two fingers' width between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is stung by the bee at the base of the shoulders after being reset in its place, then wrap it with linen threads or a woolen cloth so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the rupture, and the cure is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not concern to extract all the members of the broken first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are great, it does not concern to put the splint before 2 days or more according to the urgency of the apotheme warm sorely;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and use this ancient method of the apothecary to restore rupture, dislocation, and twist: and that you take the flour that holds to the walls of the mill, and confound it with much eggs, and put this configuration, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the apothecary restoring the rupture in many situations, especially women and small children, for it is not too clean or too frothy.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Other methods of plastering for the restoration of fractures, dislocations, and torments: take 10 ounces of aloes, 5 ounces of mirr, 7 ounces of alechen, and, in powder, mix them with a little ostrich egg yolk; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plastering that is useful for torments: take mugwart and vismal, 5 ounces; mirr and aloes, 7 ounces; acacia, 6 ounces; and bole armenic, 10 ounces, and grind them well, and confect with egg yolk or white of an egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of plastering for joints and bones that have come loose from their places, and which soothes the pain suddenly, and the size is used to cut the bone, and restores the break: take a new lamb, and moistened it with soft milk and cooked oil, and put it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing sudden pain in an abscess, and properly treating bones.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plastering which restores broken bones: take dry leaves of the fig tree, and ground leaves of the horse chestnut, and grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for treating broken bones and reducing the remaining abscess. Take root of mullein, chamomile, violets, barley flour, and from each a little; grind them, and mix with wine, and heat the members, and apply with coriander seed water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method for treating an abscess that has grown painful when healing the limb. Take roots of mullein, flax seed, hollyhock, melilote, and benjoin, violets and chamomile, a little of each; grind them, and mix with salt water or plain water or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its need for rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that when treating a broken limb for the sake of restoring it quickly, one should use only wax and oil cerots, not any other thing, and he says that they should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should use dry things, a little warm, on the broken limb for the sake of restoring it, as we have said: myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Autre maniere d’emplaastre que vaut a lession et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismaleve, et seile igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaistre et lou lie.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Another way to make plasters that serve for pain and injury: take mugger and bird feathers of men, or penises of birds, and viscere, and make them equal in length, and grind them up, and make a plaster out of it and lay it on. And then take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has his bone come out of place; if not, take it off with your hands every few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the spot, or itchiness, or there is no rest or swelling, then take off the plaster and apply a light cloth; and take a damp sponge from the sea and dip it in water and raise it up until the itchiness stops, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	and then let the member rest for an hour, and then put on a dry cloth, moistened in water or oil, and lay it on a nut, until you are sure of the warmth;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and take away its pain, then begin again gently, and a little bit of plaster, and do not strain it so hard as before; and gently until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscesses and redness and pain and swelling are all gone, and you need to use plaster and binding, then begin again, as you did at first, to make it even.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the member does not come back of all that we have said, do not release it until after 2, 3, or 5 days, and never leave it more than 10 days, according to what is seen, as long as the break-up comes closer to the joint on the bone;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then hold it back more than before, and let it fatten its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the member is drying up rather than healing, know that the healing cannot come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	As soon as you are washed with warm water, every day, and leave it in place for a while, and release it only at mealtime.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work then cut the member so that it does not continue to twist; let it rest until it has healed well, and if it is painful and afraid of the work, I see nothing better than to release it and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the different ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways to break it, and the shapes are varied, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For it has fractures which are made by the impact of a spear, and the collarbone breaks all the way down to the shoulder blade, just as it did in this case; therefore this type of fracture is called "hachure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear breaks the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two great or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact from within, or a fracture, or a collarbone of stone, or a blow on the stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches but does not touch the tendon which is outside the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has penetrated deep into the bone, as thin as a hair, and for this reason it is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by a stone or by a blow or by a similar thing, and it enters the bone, and the head of the bone is as thin as hair, so that it is called "capillary"; if it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to people who have soft bones, like children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And these breaks occur in various ways, as small pieces of stone do, and I will speak about them in their own time.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures from the traction on them, and the examination of the tents, and from the corrupt cart which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is caused by what happens when you discover bone and rub it up, so open the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for fracture, take care of accidents due to disease, and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of feeling, extension, paleness, fever, and hairs standing on end, and other similar signs in many cases, it is impossible to heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any hopeful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navel comes first to you, and it is in winter, if it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at noon.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the springtime, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone does not corrode, and the accident that we have described comes about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the tissue that covers the skull, then you should split the broken piece in half: and it is that you squeeze the chief of the sick navret, and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the pain of the wound comes when the bone is uncovered, or incision in the head, help yourself to what you need, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest as long as the abscess is calm, and are certain of the evacuation of blood; then begin to cut into the bone, and it is done according to .ij. ways of work: one way that you hold the end of the bone narrow before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	and then I bottle another length greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have different lengths of blades, some narrow and others wide, and are pointed, and made of iron; and in work lightly, so that you do not blight the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, so that you pierce it from within, as well as you provide blades with tangles, not completely sharp than it pierces through the bone at the tip, and you must have above the point a margin or 1/4 circle, so that does not pass the point beyond the bone; and you need to have more than one, so that each comes in its place at the end of the bone's tip, so that you have tangles for all test; and this is the form of the 3 ways of tangles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	Here is the translation of the text:
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if it seems to you that you should hold back the aplastic which is kept by the bone from all other instrument resembling an incision tool, but it is necessary that it be more soft and more subtle than the other incision tool;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it does not hold back any small bones, nor any scales, if the bone is lightly held by some instruments; then heal the wound with the medicines and herbs that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to work is that which Galen says, which is more effective; and press it very hard, and this is his word:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens widely, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will set the head of this lens-shaped incision.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and the part is wet on 1/2 sides, so that the cutting goes around the bone; then pound with a small mallet on it, so that you gently chip the bone all around, and take great care of the splint that is wet.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, so chip the bone lightly, for if the bone is hurt badly, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not pierce up to the skin, and the bone is cut only as much as necessary from above, and there are small pieces, then realize that sharpness, and remove the scales with a sharp razor, of which you must have different quantities, to adapt them according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are facing great razors, and then more subtle ones, do not stop doing this as long as it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle cuts, you should bring about treatment according to his healing; and this is something that has not yet been answered to those who have put their studies in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is infected, you should take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and dip it in oil, and put it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled cloth, or two, dip it in wine and oil, and put it on top of the first; and do this lighter than you can, so as not to harm the wound, then place a third linen cloth on top, and hold it in place only as long as it covers the wound;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and let it be so.i. jor or .ij., as long as the apotheces are calm, then remove it, and administer medications as if roots of herbs, and flour of times, and incense powder, and aristologue, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer medications with great fear without stinging;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound be clean, so you do not allow it to get dirty, nor do you allow dirt to get in between, for when bowels gather together on the cloth of the skull, if they corrode and decay, then they cause great harm to the patient; because when one puts a mordant medicine on, if it burns from above, then it hurts very much.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care, so that no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if sorrow comes to the patient only because of the medicine that has been put on him, which has virtue, then you should press a part of honey and 2 parts of rose oil and glue 1 drapelet onto it;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the cure with methods that he knows, until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the .ij. parts of the neck above are not broken ever by the alone force, for these are .ij. bones; and this bone is cartilaginous and does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the .ij. parts is broken, then you should put your little finger or thumb on the neck, and make it even by turning it to the side, until the neck returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do so lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his break is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot return to its place, know that you should put it equal to the head of a small ray.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if his break is in two parts, do not restore him the first day, unless you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If he does not improve after the seventh or eighth day, when the abscess has subsided a little, then bind it with linen bandages to the neck, if his break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other with the other, if his break is there also; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the apertures of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said that one should not dry the tents in hay, and each day. I do not think this is good, but it is necessary that they be wet in the making of cow dung and millstone powder; then leave the tent, until the bones are hard and the joints endure.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never do you put goose feathers in tents, and if it is a foul drape, and the wind holds it back, and blows the patient among; or make like so.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes while you are operating, if you put cotton or cotton wadding wet with oil, or a little of the liquid from the squint.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess comes while you are operating, if you put plaster on the outside, of flour made from barley, and powder of incense, cooked with cow dung, then put it on light bandages, and do not tie the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if it breaks at the nose, it is broken into small pieces, so extract with appropriate tools, then cut it and treat things that cause pain, and bind, as plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no pain within the nose, then treat tenderness, and place leeches, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken, and there is no pain within it, and the fracture is only slight, and is not broken into two pieces, except that it may be twisted inside, so that it can be adjusted lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, put your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if it is on the left jaw, put your index finger from the right hand inside lightly and make the same gesture with the other hand away, and equalize.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is misaligned by .iij., it is necessary that you bring the extension of .iij. parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the mandible causes a ruture, if it is straining on a gold or silver or silk thread, then put the cerot on the broken mandible and put 1 double sheet; and put a big, well-made piece of leather on top of the cerot, long and wide according to the mandible, and fasten it with the thread you have, and order the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure is changing, if you let it rest for three days, and then put back what has changed; and apply plaster to it, of the powder from the mill with a lot of egg or flour of sisament, after which you have removed the cerot; and put on top another light plaster, and if the applying of the plaster is successful, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healthy; many times it becomes healthy in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, administer as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not remove any piece of bone; if subtle, use appropriate instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have joined all the bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, and put on it plasters appropriate to this, to keep it closed, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the fire
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	before the shoulder, and it is broken several times, in two ways: or it is broken and dislocated in one way, and has parts, and is easy to restore; or it is broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work if it is without a wound, so that you have 2 ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that is broken with the fire; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make even the break on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have a need to extend further, so put a round staff of cloth or other material around the shoulder, or is large according to your need; and are raised and held the fire, and draws the staff towards your hand, so that you make even the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder away from the opposite side, so that it comes out completely, then the patient should lie down on his back and put a towel around his neck, and bend the arm toward the body, so that the bones of the shoulder come together;
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the fracture on your side, and if you find it difficult to split it, then you must split it; draw the pieces apart slightly, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then remove the instrument from one of the incisions that you have made, but keep the splint on the bone for healing.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should be like a spoon, and is not too thick, and should be as wide as the bone requires and the work permits; and it has 1.5 inches, if you see fit, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, just as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you split the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of the incisions, if the wound is hot, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt about the incision, if you employ the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses arise, let them be moistened with oil mixed with astringent herbs and wine, and apply to them.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	For the extraction of bone, when it is sore with plasters and scars, let them be applied with a paste made from flour and alum, and apply light staples to it, and put a spike in the socket, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very long bandage about a palm wide, then put double drapeils on staples, and plaster it; then take a thin stick two fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage is stuck;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the stake on the break, and turn the bandage over the collar, and fasten the stake on the arm; and remove it from each part, and when you see that the hour is right, and you clearly see that the stake does not move from the bone, then release it every day, and when you feel that it no longer holds,
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and raise the shoulder with a small bend of the elbow, to lift the dislocation up; thus will the break be easier to fix with the alignment of the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and so the bad accident will not come back for as long as 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then start the treatment again if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it like this, until he has recovered; and it is recovered in up to 26 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For the shoulder break
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone comes forward, and does not sever the cur, then do as we have said in the breaking of the jaw to calm an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	of the breaking of the piece in the middle, but it often breaks at the end; and when it is broken in the middle, if it declines towards the cur, and causes great pain to the patient, and lack of breath, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the vessels in the broken bone, and feels a good sensation.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then restore it as the patient lies on his back, and places him between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and connects the ribs with hands, and subtly fixes them in all ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then wrap it in a light cloth, and fasten it to the bone with a simple bandage, or salt, or any other lighter thing, and place it over the broken bone so that it does not move; and tie the cloth gently to the back, and hold it in place, and loosen it every hour, and if it relaxes, let it go, and remove the bandage, and apply treatment in the manner of cures; then remove the bandage, and hold it in place until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	regarding the rupture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I understand that the rupture of the ribs comes only from the back, and into the middle, and do not bend much except for those who are shiny; and it hurts when probed.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then restore them so that you make the rupture even, if it is right. And then put on plaster, and tighten it with a strap, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the ribs are broken and turn inward, the patient feels great pain and chills, as if they were crying, because the bone is pressing against the membrane; and it makes them weak, and they vomit a lot of blood, and it is bad for their health, and the old ones have difficulty breathing.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if from these who serve that it comes to administer meats that swell the belly, to drive out the wind to the other way.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, that hot poultices do not come, if it has not come yet.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the patient be warm.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that putting vials on the head, to draw away the wind, is reasonable; however, doubt exists that the vials do not attract excesses to the head due to weakness in the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And said neither of them that one must cover the place of another wet in oil hot, and put tents between the ribs to put equal the space around, then is cured by the cure of plague, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because the bone points to the towel, and the patient has doubt, then it is necessary to split on top of his place of the ribs broken, and it is necessary to put a tool like a weapon; and then it is necessary to cut the bones, and draw lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is big, and cure with ointments until he gets better. And if abscesses come out, then put on drapes wet in rose oil, and put on his place; and heal while his place heals that of him who has an abscess, and let it rest on his ribs where he needs to, until he gets better.
de la brisure dou col	for the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes to break the neck, and it has that he weeps; and also on the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Et when there is none, and you can see whether it will heal or not, if take heed to see that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, then they don't bleed. Know that he is mortal in many states, and if they are silent and feel well when they are extracted and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is healed, if one puts cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when there is none, and you can see whether it will heal or not, take heed to see that his hands are soft, and swollen, and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, then they don't bleed. Know that he is mortal in many states, and if they are silent and feel well when they are extracted and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is healed, if one puts cure on it. And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you can see whether it will heal or not, if take heed to see that his joints are soft, and that the accident which is in his hands, and on his back wind comes and excretes without will; and when he is sovined on his belly, then excretes without will. And when he is sovined on his back and he wants to get up, then he can't. Know that it is mortal: do not work any more in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if similar things do not come to the spine of the back, then this thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is such that if there is an abscess, put oil of rosin or oil of mouse's milk on it until it is calmed down; then put one of the poultices comforting and drying on it, and tie it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep in that part where he feels pain until he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is loose, then cover it with the poultice; and set the bone, then join the 20 lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment of charr, until it is well; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the bone," take your poultice with your left hand, and put it flat against the other hand at your will, then put on the poultice and stake it down, if you need to; then tie it up, and if there are any bones that have come loose, then cut them off, and cure the wound until it is well.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hip bone is broken, and if it has, there will be a little shortening at the top; and slant it downward, and set it to one side, and there will be pain and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it as long as you are on top of it; and know which is the fracture and its form; and if the fracture is in the head joint, so make the fracture equal, as long as it is in the natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or declines inwardly, then make the sick person lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture is arranged for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, put it on a beam, then put a board across the beam, and tighten the fracture so that it does not move; and fasten the joints with nails, as long as the place is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses are hot, if they have not been pricked, as long as the abscesses are calm, and put on that which we have said before; and then return to healing, and hold them as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And the two joints of the shoulder, and let them rise up, and cut the patient on one side; then put the knife on a heavy thing or on a table, and cut down upon it, then place the dislocated head on a board, then put the dislocated head on the table, and hold it with your hand; then cut off the dislocated head with the knife, until it returns to where it should be.
